         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_house_in_the_south_of_Sanaa_12-6-2015-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Destroyed_house_in_the_south_of_Sanaa_12-6-2015-3.jpg/220px-Destroyed_house_in_the_south_of_Sanaa_12-6-2015-3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Destroyed_house_in_the_south_of_Sanaa_12-6-2015-3.jpg/330px-Destroyed_house_in_the_south_of_Sanaa_12-6-2015-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Destroyed_house_in_the_south_of_Sanaa_12-6-2015-3.jpg/440px-Destroyed_house_in_the_south_of_Sanaa_12-6-2015-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4128" data-file-height="3096"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi-led air strike</a> on Sana'a, 12 June 2015: Saudi Arabia is operating without a UN mandate
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The 2011 Yemeni revolution followed other <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> mass protests in early 2011. The uprising was initially against unemployment, economic conditions, and corruption, as well as against the government's proposals to modify the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Yemen" title="Constitution of Yemen">constitution of Yemen</a> so that Saleh's son could inherit the presidency. </p>
      <p>In March 2011, police snipers opened fire on a pro-democracy camp in Sana'a, killing more than 50 people. In May, dozens were killed in clashes between troops and tribal fighters in Sana'a. By this point, Saleh began to lose international support. In October 2011, Yemeni human rights activist <a href="/wiki/Tawakul_Karman" class="mw-redirect" title="Tawakul Karman">Tawakul Karman</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> condemned the violence and called for a transfer of power. On 23 November 2011, Saleh flew to Riyadh, in neighbouring Saudi Arabia, to sign the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Co-operation_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf Co-operation Council">Gulf Co-operation Council</a> plan for political transition, which he had previously spurned. Upon signing the document, he agreed to legally transfer the office and powers of the presidency to his deputy, Vice President <a href="/wiki/Abdrabbuh_Mansur_Hadi" title="Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi">Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi</a>. </p>
      <p>Hadi took office for a two-year term upon winning the uncontested presidential elections in February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis_2012_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis_2012-264">[264]</a></sup> A unity government â including a prime minister from the opposition â was formed. Al-Hadi would oversee the drafting of a new constitution, followed by parliamentary and presidential elections in 2014. Saleh returned in February 2012. In the face of objections from thousands of street protesters, parliament granted him full immunity from prosecution. Saleh's son, General <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Ali_Abdullah_Saleh" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahmed Ali Abdullah Saleh">Ahmed Ali Abdullah Saleh</a>, continues to exercise a strong hold on sections of the military and security forces. </p>
      <p>AQAP claimed responsibility for a February 2012 suicide attack on the presidential palace that killed 26 Republican Guards on the day that President Hadi was sworn in. AQAP was also behind a suicide bombing that killed 96 soldiers in Sana'a three months later. In September 2012, a car bomb attack in Sana'a killed 11 people, a day after a local al-Qaeda leader <a href="/wiki/Said_al-Shihri" class="mw-redirect" title="Said al-Shihri">Said al-Shihri</a> was reported killed in the south. </p>
      <p>By 2012, there has been a "small contingent of U.S. special-operations troops" â in addition to CIA and "unofficially acknowledged" U.S. military presence â in response to increasing terror attacks by AQAP on Yemeni citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> Many analysts have pointed out the former Yemeni government role in cultivating terrorist activity in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> Following the election of the new President, <a href="/wiki/Abdrabbuh_Mansur_Hadi" title="Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi">Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi</a>, the Yemeni military was able to push <a href="/wiki/Ansar_al-Sharia_(Yemen)" title="Ansar al-Sharia (Yemen)">Ansar al-Sharia</a> back and recapture the <a href="/wiki/Shabwah_Governorate" title="Shabwah Governorate">Shabwah Governorate</a>. </p>
      <p>The central government in Sana'a remained weak, staving off challenges from <a href="/wiki/South_Yemen_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="South Yemen Movement">southern separatists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Houthis" class="mw-redirect" title="Houthis">Shia rebels</a> as well as AQAP. The <a href="/wiki/Shia_insurgency_in_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia insurgency in Yemen">Shia insurgency</a> intensified after Hadi took power, escalating in September 2014 as anti-government forces led by <a href="/wiki/Abdul-Malik_al-Houthi" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdul-Malik al-Houthi">Abdul-Malik al-Houthi</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sana%27a_(2014)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Sana'a (2014)">swept into the capital</a> and forced Hadi to agree to a "unity" government.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> The Houthis then refused to participate in the government,<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> although they continued to apply pressure on Hadi and his ministers, even shelling the president's private residence and placing him under house arrest,<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> until the government's mass resignation in January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> The following month, the Houthis dissolved parliament and <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Yemeni_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" class="mw-redirect" title="2014â15 Yemeni coup d'Ã©tat">declared</a> that a <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Committee_(Yemen)" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolutionary Committee (Yemen)">Revolutionary Committee</a> under <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Ali_al-Houthi" title="Mohammed Ali al-Houthi">Mohammed Ali al-Houthi</a> was the interim authority in Yemen. Abdul-Malik al-Houthi, a cousin of the new acting president, called the takeover a "glorious revolution." However, the "constitutional declaration" of 6 February 2015 was widely rejected by opposition politicians and foreign governments, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-glorious_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glorious-24">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yemeni_Civil_War.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Yemeni_Civil_War.svg/280px-Yemeni_Civil_War.svg.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Yemeni_Civil_War.svg/420px-Yemeni_Civil_War.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Yemeni_Civil_War.svg/560px-Yemeni_Civil_War.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1625" data-file-height="1061"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yemeni_Civil_War.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#cae7c4; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Controlled by <a href="/wiki/Houthis" class="mw-redirect" title="Houthis">Houthis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ali_Abdullah_Saleh" title="Ali Abdullah Saleh">Saleh</a> loyalists
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#f98787; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Controlled by Saudi-backed <a href="/wiki/Abdrabbuh_Mansur_Hadi" title="Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi">Hadi</a> loyalists
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#ffffff; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Controlled by <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_the_Arabian_Peninsula" title="Al-Qaeda in the Arabian Peninsula">al-Qaeda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a>-affiliated <a href="/wiki/Ansar_al-Sharia_(Yemen)" title="Ansar al-Sharia (Yemen)">Ansar al-Sharia</a>
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#e3d975; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Controlled by the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a>-backed <a href="/wiki/Southern_Transitional_Council" title="Southern Transitional Council">Southern Transitional Council</a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hadi managed to flee from Sana'a to Aden, his hometown and stronghold in <a href="/wiki/South_Yemen" title="South Yemen">the south</a>, on 21 February 2015. He promptly gave a televised speech rescinding his resignation, condemning the coup, and calling for recognition as the constitutional president of Yemen.<sup id="cite_ref-withdraw_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-withdraw-271">[271]</a></sup> The following month, Hadi declared Aden Yemen's "temporary" capital.<sup id="cite_ref-aden_dw_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aden_dw-272">[272]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> The Houthis, however, rebuffed an initiative by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a> and continued to move south toward Aden. All U.S. personnel were evacuated and President Hadi was forced to flee the country to Saudi Arabia. On 26 March 2015, Saudi Arabia announced <a href="/wiki/Operation_Decisive_Storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Decisive Storm">Operation Decisive Storm</a> and began airstrikes and announced its intentions to lead a military coalition against the <a href="/wiki/Houthis" class="mw-redirect" title="Houthis">Houthis</a>, whom they claimed were being aided by <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, and began a force buildup along the Yemeni border. The coalition included the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>. The United States announced that it was assisting with intelligence, targeting, and logistics. Saudi Arabia and Egypt would not rule out ground operations. After Hadi troops took control of Aden from Houthis, jihadist groups became active in the city, and some terrorist incidents were linked to them such as <a href="/wiki/Missionaries_of_Charity_attack_in_Aden" title="Missionaries of Charity attack in Aden">Missionaries of Charity attack in Aden</a> on 4 March 2016. Since February 2018, Aden has been <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aden_(2018)" title="Battle of Aden (2018)">seized</a> by the UAE-backed separatist <a href="/wiki/Southern_Transitional_Council" title="Southern Transitional Council">Southern Transitional Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>More than 50,000 children in Yemen died from starvation in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Famine_in_Yemen_(2016%E2%80%93present)" title="Famine in Yemen (2016âpresent)">famine in Yemen</a> is the direct result of the Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen and <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_Yemen" title="Blockade of Yemen">blockade of Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> The famine is being compounded by an outbreak of <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> that has affected more than one million people.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Yemen" title="Geography of Yemen">Geography of Yemen</a>

      <p>Yemen is in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>, in the southern part of the Arabian Peninsula,<sup id="cite_ref-Burrows2010_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burrows2010-281">[281]</a></sup> It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> to <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia%E2%80%93Yemen_border" title="Saudi ArabiaâYemen border">the north</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> to the west, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden" title="Gulf of Aden">Gulf of Aden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guardafui_Channel" title="Guardafui Channel">Guardafui Channel</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a> to <a href="/wiki/Oman%E2%80%93Yemen_border" title="OmanâYemen border">the east</a>. between latitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_parallel_north" title="12th parallel north">12</a> and <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_north" title="19th parallel north">19Â°N</a> and longitudes <a href="/wiki/42nd_meridian_east" title="42nd meridian east">42</a> and <a href="/wiki/55th_meridian_east" title="55th meridian east">55Â°E</a>. Yemen is at 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994658806"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Yemen&amp;params=15_N_48_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">15Â°N</span> <span class="longitude">48Â°E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">ï»¿ / ï»¿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">15Â°N 48Â°E</span><span style="display:none">ï»¿ / <span class="geo">15; 48</span></span></span></a></span>, and is 527,970&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (203,850&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in size. </p>
      <p>A number of Red Sea islands, including the <a href="/wiki/Hanish_Islands" title="Hanish Islands">Hanish Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kamaran" title="Kamaran">Kamaran</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Perim" title="Perim">Perim</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Socotra" title="Socotra">Socotra</a> in the Arabian Sea, belong to Yemen; the largest of these is <a href="/wiki/Socotra" title="Socotra">Socotra</a>. Many of the islands are volcanic; for example <a href="/wiki/Jabal_al-Tair_island" class="mw-redirect" title="Jabal al-Tair island">Jabal al-Tair</a> had a volcanic eruption in 2007, and before that in 1883. Although mainland Yemen is in the southern Arabian Peninsula and thus part of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, and its <a href="/wiki/Hanish_Islands" title="Hanish Islands">Hanish Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Perim" title="Perim">Perim</a> in the Red Sea are associated with Asia, the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of Socotra, which lies east of the horn of <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and is much closer to Africa than to Asia, is geographically and biogeographically associated with Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> Socotra faces the <a href="/wiki/Guardafui_Channel" title="Guardafui Channel">Guardafui Channel</a> and the Somali Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions_and_climate">Regions and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Regions and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">

           <a href="/wiki/File:Water_reservoir,_yemen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Water_reservoir%2C_yemen.jpg/200px-Water_reservoir%2C_yemen.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Water_reservoir%2C_yemen.jpg/300px-Water_reservoir%2C_yemen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Water_reservoir%2C_yemen.jpg/400px-Water_reservoir%2C_yemen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           A water reservoir in <a href="/wiki/Jabal_Haraz" title="Jabal Haraz">Jabal Haraz</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Haraz_200612_Yemen-115_(353667843).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Haraz_200612_Yemen-115_%28353667843%29.jpg/200px-Haraz_200612_Yemen-115_%28353667843%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Haraz_200612_Yemen-115_%28353667843%29.jpg/300px-Haraz_200612_Yemen-115_%28353667843%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Haraz_200612_Yemen-115_%28353667843%29.jpg/400px-Haraz_200612_Yemen-115_%28353667843%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           A terraced side of one of the Haraz Mountains in <a href="/wiki/Al_Mahwit_Governorate" title="Al Mahwit Governorate">Al Mahwit Governorate</a> near <a href="/wiki/Jabal_An-Nabi_Shu%27ayb" title="Jabal An-Nabi Shu'ayb">Jabal An-Nabi Shu'ayb</a> (the highest mountain in the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a>), west of <a href="/wiki/Sanaa" title="Sanaa">Sanaa</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Yemen can be divided geographically into four main regions: the coastal plains in the west, the western highlands, the eastern highlands, and the <a href="/wiki/Rub%27_al_Khali" title="Rub' al Khali">Rub' al Khali</a> in the east. The <a href="/wiki/Tihamah" title="Tihamah">TihÄmah</a> ("hot lands" or "hot earth") form a very arid and flat coastal plain along Yemen's entire Red Sea coastline. Despite the aridity, the presence of many lagoons makes this region very marshy and a suitable breeding ground for <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> <a href="/wiki/Mosquito" title="Mosquito">mosquitos</a>. Extensive crescent-shaped sand dunes are present. The evaporation in the Tihamah is so great that streams from the highlands never reach the sea, but they do contribute to extensive <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a> reserves. Today, these are heavily exploited for agricultural use. Near the village of <a href="/wiki/Madar,_Yemen" title="Madar, Yemen">Madar</a> about 50&nbsp;km (30&nbsp;mi) north of Sana'a, <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaur</a> footprints were found, indicating that the area was once a muddy flat. The Tihamah ends abruptly at the <a href="/wiki/Escarpment" title="Escarpment">escarpment</a> of the western highlands. This area, now heavily <a href="/wiki/Terrace_(agriculture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrace (agriculture)">terraced</a> to meet the demand for food, receives the highest rainfall in Arabia, rapidly increasing from 100&nbsp;mm (3.9&nbsp;in) per year to about 760&nbsp;mm (29.9&nbsp;in) in Taiz and over 1,000&nbsp;mm (39.4&nbsp;in) in Ibb. Temperatures are warm in the day but fall dramatically at night. Perennial streams occur in the highlands, but these never reach the sea because of high evaporation in the Tihamah.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The central highlands are an extensive high plateau over 2,000&nbsp;m (6,562&nbsp;ft) in elevation. This area is drier than the western highlands because of rain-shadow influences, but still receives sufficient rain in wet years for extensive cropping. Water storage allows for <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> and the growing of <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>. Sana'a is in this region. The highest point in Yemen and Arabia is <a href="/wiki/Jabal_An-Nabi_Shu%27ayb" title="Jabal An-Nabi Shu'ayb">Jabal An-Nabi Shu'ayb</a>, at about 3,666&nbsp;m (12,028&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Burrows2010_281-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burrows2010-281">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Laughlin2008_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laughlin2008-284">[284]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Yemen's portion of the Rub al Khali desert in the east is much lower, generally below 1,000&nbsp;m (3,281&nbsp;ft), and receives almost no rain. It is populated only by <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> herders of <a href="/wiki/Dromedary" title="Dromedary">camels</a>. The growing scarcity of water is a source of increasing international concern. See <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Yemen" title="Water supply and sanitation in Yemen">Water supply and sanitation in Yemen</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Yemen" title="Wildlife of Yemen">Wildlife of Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Dragon_Blood_Tree,_Socotra_Island_(10098980413).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Dragon_Blood_Tree%2C_Socotra_Island_%2810098980413%29.jpg/200px-Dragon_Blood_Tree%2C_Socotra_Island_%2810098980413%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Dragon_Blood_Tree%2C_Socotra_Island_%2810098980413%29.jpg/300px-Dragon_Blood_Tree%2C_Socotra_Island_%2810098980413%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Dragon_Blood_Tree%2C_Socotra_Island_%2810098980413%29.jpg/400px-Dragon_Blood_Tree%2C_Socotra_Island_%2810098980413%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="4016"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <i><a href="/wiki/Dracaena_cinnabari" title="Dracaena cinnabari">Dracaena cinnabari</a></i> at <a href="/wiki/Socotra_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Socotra Island">Socotra Island</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:South_Arabian_-_A_Lion_and_a_Leopard_Attacking_Animals_-_Walters_2171.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/South_Arabian_-_A_Lion_and_a_Leopard_Attacking_Animals_-_Walters_2171.jpg/200px-South_Arabian_-_A_Lion_and_a_Leopard_Attacking_Animals_-_Walters_2171.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="109" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/South_Arabian_-_A_Lion_and_a_Leopard_Attacking_Animals_-_Walters_2171.jpg/300px-South_Arabian_-_A_Lion_and_a_Leopard_Attacking_Animals_-_Walters_2171.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/South_Arabian_-_A_Lion_and_a_Leopard_Attacking_Animals_-_Walters_2171.jpg/400px-South_Arabian_-_A_Lion_and_a_Leopard_Attacking_Animals_-_Walters_2171.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1798" data-file-height="976"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           A <a href="/wiki/South_Arabia" title="South Arabia">South Arabian</a> relief from the 5th century BC, in <a href="/wiki/Walters_Art_Museum" title="Walters Art Museum">Walters Art Museum</a>. On the left side of this relief, a <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_lion" title="Asiatic lion">lion</a> attacks a <a href="/wiki/Gazelle" title="Gazelle">gazelle</a>, while a <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">rabbit</a> tries to jump away from the gazelle's forelegs. On the right, a <a href="/wiki/Arabian_leopard" title="Arabian leopard">leopard</a> jumps down from rocks onto the back of an <a href="/wiki/Ibex" title="Ibex">ibex</a>; a small <a href="/wiki/Rodent" title="Rodent">rodent</a> flees the hoofs of the ibex. Birds in the branches of <i><a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">acacia</a></i> trees observe the two scenes.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Yemen contains six terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula_coastal_fog_desert" title="Arabian Peninsula coastal fog desert">Arabian Peninsula coastal fog desert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socotra_Island_xeric_shrublands" title="Socotra Island xeric shrublands">Socotra Island xeric shrublands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Arabian_foothills_savanna" title="Southwestern Arabian foothills savanna">Southwestern Arabian foothills savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Arabian_montane_woodlands" title="Southwestern Arabian montane woodlands">Southwestern Arabian montane woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Desert" title="Arabian Desert">Arabian Desert</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea_Nubo-Sindian_tropical_desert_and_semi-desert" title="Red Sea Nubo-Sindian tropical desert and semi-desert">Red Sea Nubo-Sindian tropical desert and semi-desert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-285">[285]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The flora of Yemen is a mixture of the tropical African, Sudanian plant geographical region and the <b>Saharo-Arabian region</b>. The Sudanian elementâcharacterized by relatively high rainfallâdominates the western mountains and parts of the highland plains. The Saharo-Arabian element dominates in the coastal plains, eastern mountain, and the eastern and northern desert plains. A high percentage of Yemen plants belong to tropical African plants of Sudanian regions. Among the Sudanian element species, the following may be mentioned: <i><a href="/wiki/Ficus" title="Ficus">Ficus</a></i> spp., <i><a href="/wiki/Acacia_mellifera" class="mw-redirect" title="Acacia mellifera">Acacia mellifera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grewia_villosa" title="Grewia villosa">Grewia villosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commiphora" title="Commiphora">Commiphora</a></i> spp., <i><a href="/wiki/Rose" title="Rose">Rosa</a> abyssinica</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cadaba" title="Cadaba">Cadaba</a> farinosa</i> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup> Among the Saharo-Arabian species, these may be mentioned: <i><a href="/wiki/Panicum_turgidum" title="Panicum turgidum">Panicum turgidum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aerva_javanica" title="Aerva javanica">Aerva javanica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zygophyllum" title="Zygophyllum">Zygophyllum</a> simplex, <a href="/wiki/Fagonia" title="Fagonia">Fagonia</a> indica, <a href="/wiki/Salsola" title="Salsola">Salsola</a></i> spp., <i><a href="/wiki/Acacia_tortilis" class="mw-redirect" title="Acacia tortilis">Acacia tortilis</a>, A. hamulos, <a href="/wiki/Acacia_ehrenbergiana" class="mw-redirect" title="Acacia ehrenbergiana">A. ehrenbergiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_dactylifera" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenix dactylifera">Phoenix dactylifera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyphaene_thebaica" title="Hyphaene thebaica">Hyphaene thebaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capparis_decidua" title="Capparis decidua">Capparis decidua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvadora_persica" title="Salvadora persica">Salvadora persica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balanites_aegyptiaca" title="Balanites aegyptiaca">Balanites aegyptiaca</a></i>, and many others. Many of the Saharo-Arabian species are endemic to the extensive sandy coastal plain (the Tihamah).<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> The characteristic genera of the Irano-Turanian in the eastern and northern east of the country are: <i><a href="/wiki/Calligonum" title="Calligonum">Calligonum</a></i> spp., <i><a href="/wiki/Cymbopogon" title="Cymbopogon">Cymbopogon</a> jwarancusa</i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Tamarix" title="Tamarix">Tamarix</a></i> spp. and of the Mediterranean regions are: <i><a href="/wiki/Teucrium" title="Teucrium">Teucrium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lavandula" title="Lavandula">Lavandula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juniperus" class="mw-redirect" title="Juniperus">Juniperus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brassica" title="Brassica">Brassica</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Diplotaxis_(plant)" title="Diplotaxis (plant)">Diplotaxis</a></i> spp.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Among the fauna, the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_leopard" title="Arabian leopard">Arabian leopard</a>, which would inhabit the mountains, is considered rare here.<sup id="cite_ref-SpaltonHikmani2006_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpaltonHikmani2006-288">[288]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Yemen" title="Environmental issues in Yemen">Environmental issues in Yemen</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Environmental_issues_in_Yemen&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <div class="thumb tright">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg/220px-Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg/330px-Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg/440px-Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1320"></a> 
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a href="/wiki/File:Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
           </div>Shibam Wadi Hadhramaut Yemen
          </div>
         </div>
        </div> <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues" title="Environmental issues">Environmental issues</a> in Yemen are abundant and are divided into the categories of land and water. In the aspect of water, Yemen has limited natural fresh water resources and inadequate supplies of potable water. As for the land, two main issues of Yemen are <a href="/wiki/Overgrazing" title="Overgrazing">overgrazing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>. Yemen has signed several international agreements: Climate Change-<a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a>, Desertification, Endangered Species, Environmental Modification, Hazardous Wastes, <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_Sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Law of the Sea">Law of the Sea</a>, and Ozone Layer Protection.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_issues_in_Yemen_auto_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_issues_in_Yemen_auto-289">[289]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Yemen" title="Politics of Yemen">Politics of Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Yemen is a republic with a <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> legislature. Under the 1991 constitution, an elected president, an elected 301-seat <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Representatives_of_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Assembly of Representatives of Yemen">Assembly of Representatives</a>, and an appointed 111-member <a href="/wiki/Shura" title="Shura">Shura</a> Council share power. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Yemen" title="President of Yemen">President</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Yemen" title="Prime Minister of Yemen">Prime Minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. In Sana'a, a <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Political_Council" title="Supreme Political Council">Supreme Political Council</a> (not recognized internationally) forms the government. </p>
      <p>The 1991 constitution provides that the president be elected by popular vote from at least two candidates endorsed by at least 15 members of the Parliament. The prime minister, in turn, is appointed by the president and must be approved by two-thirds of the Parliament. The presidential term of office is seven years, and the parliamentary term of elected office is six years. <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">Suffrage</a> is universal for people age 18 and older, but only Muslims may hold elected office.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>President <a href="/wiki/Ali_Abdullah_Saleh" title="Ali Abdullah Saleh">Ali Abdullah Saleh</a> became the first elected President in reunified Yemen in 1999 (though he had been President of unified Yemen since 1990 and president of North Yemen since 1978). He was re-elected to office in September 2006. Saleh's victory was marked by an election that international observers judged was "partly free," though the election was accompanied by violence, violations of press freedoms, and allegations of fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> Parliamentary elections were held in April 2003, and the <a href="/wiki/General_People%27s_Congress_(Yemen)" title="General People's Congress (Yemen)">General People's Congress</a> maintained an absolute majority. Saleh remained almost uncontested in his seat of power until 2011, when local frustration at his refusal to hold another round of elections, as combined with the impact of the 2011 Arab Spring, resulted in mass protests.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis_2012_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis_2012-264">[264]</a></sup> In 2012, he was forced to resign from power, though he remained an important actor in Yemeni politics, allying with the <a href="/wiki/Houthis" class="mw-redirect" title="Houthis">Houthis</a> during their takeover in the mid-2010s.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The constitution calls for an independent judiciary. The former northern and southern legal codes have been unified. The legal system includes separate commercial courts and a Supreme Court based in Sana'a. <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a> is the main source of laws, with many court cases being debated according to the religious basis of law and many judges being religious scholars as well as legal authorities. The Prison Authority Organization Act, Republican decree no. 48 (1981), and Prison Act regulations, provide the legal framework for management of the country's prison system.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Yemen" title="Foreign relations of Yemen">Foreign relations of Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ali_Abdullah_Saleh_meets_Donald_H._Rumsfeld_at_Pentagon_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ali_Abdullah_Saleh_meets_Donald_H._Rumsfeld_at_Pentagon_2004.jpg/220px-Ali_Abdullah_Saleh_meets_Donald_H._Rumsfeld_at_Pentagon_2004.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ali_Abdullah_Saleh_meets_Donald_H._Rumsfeld_at_Pentagon_2004.jpg/330px-Ali_Abdullah_Saleh_meets_Donald_H._Rumsfeld_at_Pentagon_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ali_Abdullah_Saleh_meets_Donald_H._Rumsfeld_at_Pentagon_2004.jpg/440px-Ali_Abdullah_Saleh_meets_Donald_H._Rumsfeld_at_Pentagon_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ali_Abdullah_Saleh_meets_Donald_H._Rumsfeld_at_Pentagon_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former Yemeni President <a href="/wiki/Ali_Abdullah_Saleh" title="Ali Abdullah Saleh">Ali Abdullah Saleh</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">the Pentagon</a>, 8 June 2004
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The geography and ruling imams of North Yemen kept the country isolated from foreign influence before 1962. The country's relations with Saudi Arabia were defined by the <a href="/wiki/Taif_Agreement" title="Taif Agreement">Taif Agreement</a> of 1934, which delineated the northernmost part of the border between the two kingdoms and set the framework for commercial and other intercourse. The Taif Agreement has been renewed periodically in 20-year increments, and its validity was reaffirmed in 1995. Relations with the British colonial authorities in Aden and the south were usually tense. </p>
      <p>The Soviet and Chinese Aid Missions established in 1958 and 1959 were the first important non-Muslim presences in North Yemen. Following the September 1962 revolution, the <a href="/wiki/Yemen_Arab_Republic" title="Yemen Arab Republic">Yemen Arab Republic</a> became closely allied with and heavily dependent upon Egypt. Saudi Arabia aided the royalists in their attempt to defeat the Republicans and did not recognize the Yemen Arab Republic until 1970. At the same time, Saudi Arabia maintained direct contact with Yemeni tribes, which sometimes strained its official relations with the Yemeni Government. Saudi Arabia remained hostile to any form of political and social reform in Yemen<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> and continued to provide financial support for tribal elites.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In February 1989, North Yemen joined Iraq, Jordan, and Egypt in forming the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Cooperation_Council" title="Arab Cooperation Council">Arab Cooperation Council</a> (ACC), an organization created partly in response to the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a> and intended to foster closer economic cooperation and integration among its members. After unification, the Republic of Yemen was accepted as a member of the ACC in place of its YAR predecessor. In the wake of the Persian Gulf crisis, the ACC has remained inactive. Yemen is not a member of the Gulf Cooperation Council mainly for its republican government.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Yemen is a member of the United Nations, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, and also participates in the <a href="/wiki/Nonaligned_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Nonaligned movement">nonaligned movement</a>. The Republic of Yemen accepted responsibility for all treaties and debts of its predecessors, the Yemen Arab Republic (YAR) and the People's Democratic Republic of Yemen (PDRY). Yemen has acceded to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons">Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Shakes_Hands_With_Yemeni_President_Hadi_Before_Bilateral_Meeting_in_Saudi_Arabia_(17212641020).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Secretary_Kerry_Shakes_Hands_With_Yemeni_President_Hadi_Before_Bilateral_Meeting_in_Saudi_Arabia_%2817212641020%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_Shakes_Hands_With_Yemeni_President_Hadi_Before_Bilateral_Meeting_in_Saudi_Arabia_%2817212641020%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Secretary_Kerry_Shakes_Hands_With_Yemeni_President_Hadi_Before_Bilateral_Meeting_in_Saudi_Arabia_%2817212641020%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_Shakes_Hands_With_Yemeni_President_Hadi_Before_Bilateral_Meeting_in_Saudi_Arabia_%2817212641020%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Secretary_Kerry_Shakes_Hands_With_Yemeni_President_Hadi_Before_Bilateral_Meeting_in_Saudi_Arabia_%2817212641020%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_Shakes_Hands_With_Yemeni_President_Hadi_Before_Bilateral_Meeting_in_Saudi_Arabia_%2817212641020%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4208" data-file-height="2799"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Shakes_Hands_With_Yemeni_President_Hadi_Before_Bilateral_Meeting_in_Saudi_Arabia_(17212641020).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ousted Yemeni President <a href="/wiki/Abdrabbuh_Mansur_Hadi" title="Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi">Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi</a> with U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>, 7 May 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:019_Rally_(39025071401).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/019_Rally_%2839025071401%29.jpg/220px-019_Rally_%2839025071401%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="103" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/019_Rally_%2839025071401%29.jpg/330px-019_Rally_%2839025071401%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/019_Rally_%2839025071401%29.jpg/440px-019_Rally_%2839025071401%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="1814"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:019_Rally_(39025071401).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Protest against Saudi <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_Yemen" title="Blockade of Yemen">blockade of Yemen</a>, New York City, 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since the end of the 1994 civil war, tangible progress has been made on the diplomatic front in restoring normal relations with Yemen's neighbors. In the summer of 2000, Yemen and Saudi Arabia signed an International Border Treaty settling a 50-year-old dispute over the location of the border between the two countries. Until the signing of the Yemen-Saudi Arabia peace treaty in July 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> Yemen's northern border was undefined; the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Desert" title="Arabian Desert">Arabian Desert</a> prevented any human habitation there. Yemen settled its dispute with <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Hanish_Islands" title="Hanish Islands">Hanish Islands</a> in 1998. The <a href="/wiki/Saudi_%E2%80%93_Yemen_barrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Saudi â Yemen barrier">Saudi â Yemen barrier</a> was constructed by Saudi Arabia against an influx of <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Illegal immigrant">illegal immigrants</a> and against the smuggling of drugs and weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> <i>The Independent</i> headed an article with "Saudi Arabia, one of the most vocal critics in the Arab world of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>'s "security fence" in the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>, is quietly emulating the Israeli example by erecting a barrier along its porous border with Yemen."<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2020, the Trump administration and key <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">US</a>â allies, including <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, cut off tens of millions of dollars for health care programs and other aid to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>' appeal for Yemen. As a result of funding cuts, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_for_the_Coordination_of_Humanitarian_Affairs" title="United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs">United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs</a> (UNOCHA) stated that the UN agencies were forced to either close or reduce more than 75 per cent of its programs that year alone, affecting more than 8 million people. Saudi Arabia had been leading a Western-backed military coalition, including the United Arab Emirates as a key member, which intervened in Yemen in 2015, in a bid to restore the government ousted from power by the <a href="/wiki/Houthi_movement" title="Houthi movement">Houthi movement</a>. The United Nations described the situation in Yemen, where the war killed tens of thousands of people and left millions on the brink of famine, as the worldâs worst humanitarian crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Yemen" title="Human rights in Yemen">Human rights in Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The government and its security forces, often considered to suffer from rampant corruption,<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> have been responsible for torture, inhumane treatment, and extrajudicial executions. There are arbitrary arrests of citizens, especially in the south, as well as arbitrary searches of homes. Prolonged pretrial detention is a serious problem, and judicial corruption, inefficiency, and executive interference undermine due process. Freedom of speech, the press, and religion are all restricted.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> Journalists critical of the government are often harassed and threatened by the police.<sup id="cite_ref-YemenProfile2008_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YemenProfile2008-224">[224]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Yemen" title="LGBT rights in Yemen">Homosexuality</a> is illegal, punishable by death.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the start of the Shia insurgency, many people accused of supporting al-Houthi have been arrested and held without charge or trial. According to the U.S. State Department International Religious Freedom Report 2007, "Some Zaydis reported harassment and discrimination by the government because they were suspected of sympathizing with the al-Houthis. However, it appears the Government's actions against the group were probably politically, not religiously, motivated."<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/U.S._Committee_for_Refugees_and_Immigrants" title="U.S. Committee for Refugees and Immigrants">U.S. Committee for Refugees and Immigrants</a> reported several violations of <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugee</a> and asylum seekers' rights in the organization's 2008 <i>World Refugee Survey</i>. Yemeni authorities reportedly deported numerous foreigners without giving them access to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a>, despite the UN's repeated requests. Refugees further reported violence directed against them by Yemeni authorities while living in refugee camps. Yemeni officials reportedly raped and beat camp-based refugees with impunity in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-305">[305]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Yemen is ranked last of 135 countries in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Global_Gender_Gap_Report" title="Global Gender Gap Report">Global Gender Gap Report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> reported on discrimination and <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">violence against women</a> as well as on the abolition of the minimum marriage age of fifteen for women. The onset of <a href="/wiki/Puberty" title="Puberty">puberty</a> (interpreted by some to be as low as the age of nine) was set as a requirement for marriage instead.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> Publicity about the case of ten-year-old Yemeni divorcee <a href="/wiki/Nujood_Ali" title="Nujood Ali">Nujood Ali</a> brought the child marriage issue to the fore not only in Yemen but also worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Daragahi2008_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daragahi2008-308">[308]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Walt2009_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walt2009-309">[309]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Madabish2009_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Madabish2009-310">[310]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 30 June 2020, a <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> group revealed the scale of torture and deaths in Yemen's unofficial detention centres. <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi</a> forces were responsible for some of the most shocking treatment of prisoners, including being hung upside down for hours and sexual torture such as the burning of genitals.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_trafficking">Human trafficking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Human trafficking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking_in_Yemen" title="Human trafficking in Yemen">Human trafficking in Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a> 2013 <i>Trafficking in Persons</i> report classified Yemen as a Tier 3 country,<sup id="cite_ref-trafficking-in-persons-2013_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trafficking-in-persons-2013-312">[312]</a></sup> meaning that its government does not fully comply with the minimum standards against <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a> and is not making significant efforts to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-tiers-2013_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tiers-2013-313">[313]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Yemen officially abolished <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> in 1962,<sup id="cite_ref-thedailystar2004_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thedailystar2004-314">[314]</a></sup> but it is still being practiced.<sup id="cite_ref-Al-Arabiya_2010_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al-Arabiya_2010-315">[315]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 22 June 2020, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> wrote an open letter to the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary-General</a> on âChildren and Armed Conflictâ report to improve the protection of children in Yemen and in <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amnesty" title="Amnesty">Amnesty</a> said, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> must urgently fix its monitoring and reporting mechanism for children impacted by armed conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Human_Right_Watch" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Right Watch">Human Right Watch</a> on 14 September 2020, demanded the interference caused by Houthi rebels and other authorities in Yemen aid operations to stop, as millions of lives dependent on the aid operations were being put at risk.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Yemen">Military of Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Soldiers_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Soldiers_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/220px-Soldiers_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Soldiers_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/330px-Soldiers_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Soldiers_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/440px-Soldiers_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1133" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Soldiers_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Yemeni Army">Yemeni Army</a> in 2011.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The armed forces of Yemen include the <a href="/wiki/Yemen_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Yemen Army">Yemen Army</a> (includes <a href="/wiki/Republican_Guard_(Yemen)" title="Republican Guard (Yemen)">Republican Guard</a>), Navy (includes Marines), <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_Air_Force" title="Yemeni Air Force">Yemeni Air Force</a> (Al Quwwat al Jawwiya al Yamaniya; includes Air Defense Force). A major reorganization of the armed forces continues. The unified air forces and air defenses are now under one command. The navy has concentration in Aden. Total armed forces manning numbers about 401,000 active personnel, including moreover especially conscripts. The <a href="/wiki/Yemen_Arab_Republic" title="Yemen Arab Republic">Yemen Arab Republic</a> and The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Republic_of_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Democratic Republic of Yemen">People's Democratic Republic of Yemen</a> joined to form the Republic of Yemen on 22 May 1990.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The supreme commander of the armed forces is the President of the Republic of Yemen. </p>
      <p>The number of military personnel in Yemen is relatively high; in sum, Yemen has the second largest military force on the Arabian Peninsula after Saudi Arabia. In 2012, total active troops were estimated as follows: army, 390,000; navy, 7,000; and air force, 5,000. In September 2007, the government announced the reinstatement of compulsory military service. Yemen's defense budget, which in 2006 represented approximately 40 percent of the total government budget, is expected to remain high for the near term, as the military draft takes effect and internal security threats continue to escalate. By 2012, Yemen had 401,000 active personnel. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Governorates_of_Yemen" title="Governorates of Yemen">Governorates of Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Yemen_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Regions_of_Yemen_map.svg/220px-Regions_of_Yemen_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Regions_of_Yemen_map.svg/330px-Regions_of_Yemen_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Regions_of_Yemen_map.svg/440px-Regions_of_Yemen_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1210" data-file-height="730"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Map of the Federal Regions of Yemen
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Yemen,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Yemen%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/220px-Yemen%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Yemen%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/330px-Yemen%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Yemen%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/440px-Yemen%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1524" data-file-height="995"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Governorates of Yemen
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of the end of 2004, Yemen was divided into twenty governorates (<i><a href="/wiki/Muhafazat" class="mw-redirect" title="Muhafazat">muhafazat</a></i> â the latest being Raymah Governorate, which was created during 2004) plus one municipality called "Amanat Al-Asemah" (the latter containing the constitutional capital, Sana'a).<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup> An additional governorate (<a href="/wiki/Soqatra_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Soqatra Governorate">Soqatra Governorate</a>) was created in December 2013 comprising Socotra Island (bottom-right corner of map), previously part of Hadramaut Governorate.<sup id="cite_ref-Presidenthadi-gov-ye.info_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Presidenthadi-gov-ye.info-320">[320]</a></sup> The governorates are subdivided into 333 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts of Yemen">districts</a> (<i>muderiah</i>), which are subdivided into 2,210 sub-districts, and then into 38,284 villages (as of 2001). </p>
      <p>In 2014, a constitutional panel decided to divide the country into six regionsâfour in the north, two in the south, and capital Sana'a outside of any regionâcreating a federalist model of governance.<sup id="cite_ref-ajsix_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ajsix-321">[321]</a></sup> This federal proposal was a contributing factor toward the <a href="/wiki/Houthis" class="mw-redirect" title="Houthis">Houthis</a>' subsequent <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Yemeni_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" class="mw-redirect" title="2014â15 Yemeni coup d'Ã©tat">coup d'Ã©tat</a> against the government.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> </p>
