        <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Bayda_Governorate" title="Al Bayda Governorate">Al Bayda</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Shabwah_Governorate" title="Shabwah Governorate">Shabwah</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Taiz_Governorate" title="Taiz Governorate">Taiz</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Lahij_Governorate" title="Lahij Governorate">Lahij</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Abyan_Governorate" title="Abyan Governorate">Abyan</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Aden_Governorate" title="Aden Governorate">Aden</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Socotra_Governorate" title="Socotra Governorate">Socotra</a><sup id="cite_ref-Presidenthadi-gov-ye.info_320-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Presidenthadi-gov-ye.info-320">[320]</a></sup></li>
       </ol>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Yemen" title="Economy of Yemen">Economy of Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Yemen" title="Telecommunications in Yemen">Telecommunications in Yemen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation in Yemen">Transportation in Yemen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Internet_usage_in_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet usage in Yemen">Internet usage in Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yemen_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Yemen_Export_Treemap.png/330px-Yemen_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Yemen_Export_Treemap.png/495px-Yemen_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Yemen_Export_Treemap.png/660px-Yemen_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="750"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yemen_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Yemen's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Yemen as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> had a GDP (PPP) of US$61.63 billion, with an income per capita of $2,500. Services are the largest economic sector (61.4% of GDP), followed by the industrial sector (30.9%), and agriculture (7.7%). Of these, petroleum production represents around 25% of GDP and 63% of the government's revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-325">[325]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Coffee_Plantation_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Coffee_Plantation_1.jpg/220px-Coffee_Plantation_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Coffee_Plantation_1.jpg/330px-Coffee_Plantation_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Coffee_Plantation_1.jpg/440px-Coffee_Plantation_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Coffee_Plantation_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A coffee plantation in North Yemen
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Principal agricultural commodities produced in the nation include grain, vegetables, fruits, <a href="/wiki/Pulse_(legume)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulse (legume)">pulses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khat" title="Khat">qat</a>, coffee, cotton, dairy products, fish, livestock (sheep, goats, cattle, camels), and poultry.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_325-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-325">[325]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most Yemenis are employed in agriculture. However, the role of <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Agricultural sector">agricultural sector</a> is limited due to the relatively low share of the sector in GDP and the large share of net food-buying households in Yemen (97%).<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">Sorghum</a> is the most common crop. Cotton and many fruit trees are also grown, with <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mangoes</a> being the most valuable. A big problem in Yemen is the cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Khat" title="Khat">Khat</a> (or qat), a psychoactive plant that releases a <a href="/wiki/Stimulant" title="Stimulant">stimulant</a> when chewed, and accounts for up to 40 percent of the water drawn from the Sana'a Basin each year, and that figure is rising. Some agricultural practices are drying the Sana'a Basin and displaced vital crops, which has resulted in increasing <a href="/wiki/Food_prices" title="Food prices">food prices</a>. Rising food prices, in turn, pushed an additional six percent of the country into poverty in 2008 alone.<sup id="cite_ref-QatProduction_327-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QatProduction-327">[327]</a></sup> Efforts are being made by the government and <a href="/wiki/Dawoodi_Bohra" title="Dawoodi Bohra">Dawoodi Bohra</a> community at North Yemen to replace qat with coffee plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Yemen's industrial sector is centred on crude oil production and petroleum refining, food processing, handicrafts, small-scale production of cotton textiles and leather goods, aluminum products, commercial ship repair, cement, and natural gas production. In 2013, Yemen had an industrial production growth rate of 4.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_325-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-325">[325]</a></sup> It also has large proven reserves of natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup> Yemen's <a href="/wiki/Yemen_LNG" title="Yemen LNG">first liquified natural gas plant</a> began production in October 2009. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour_force">Labour force</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Labour force">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Souq@Sana%27a.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Souq%40Sana%27a.JPG/220px-Souq%40Sana%27a.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Souq%40Sana%27a.JPG/330px-Souq%40Sana%27a.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Souq%40Sana%27a.JPG/440px-Souq%40Sana%27a.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Souq@Sana%27a.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Souq" class="mw-redirect" title="Souq">Souq</a> in <a href="/wiki/Old_Sana%27a" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Sana'a">Old Sana'a</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The labor force was seven million workers in 2013. Services, industry, construction and commerce together constitute less than 25% of the labor force. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Export_and_import">Export and import</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Export and import">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, exports from Yemen totaled $6.694 billion. The main export commodities are crude oil, coffee, dried and salted fish, liquefied natural gas. These products were mainly sent to China (41%), Thailand (19.2%), India (11.4%), and South Korea (4.4%). Imports as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> total $10.97 billion. The main imported commodities are machinery and equipment, foodstuffs, livestock, and chemicals. These products were mainly imported from the EU (48.8%), UAE (9.8%), Switzerland (8.8%), China (7.4%), and India (5.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_325-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-325">[325]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_budget">State budget</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: State budget">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yemen_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Yemen_06.jpg/220px-Yemen_06.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Yemen_06.jpg/330px-Yemen_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Yemen_06.jpg/440px-Yemen_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1678" data-file-height="1169"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yemen_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Drilling for oil using a <a href="/wiki/Drilling_rig" title="Drilling rig">land rig</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Yemeni government's budget consisted of $7.769 billion in revenues and $12.31 billion in expenditures. Taxes and other revenues constituted roughly 17.7% of the GDP, with a budget deficit of 10.3%. The public debt was 47.1% of GDP. Yemen had reserves of foreign exchange and gold of around $5.538 billion in 2013. Its inflation rate over the same period based on consumer prices was 11.8%. Yemen's external debt totaled $7.806 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_325-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-325">[325]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Beginning in the mid-1950s, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and China provided large-scale assistance. For example, China and the United States are involved with the expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Sana%27a_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Sana'a International Airport">Sana'a International Airport</a>. In the south, pre-independence economic activity was overwhelmingly concentrated in the port city of Aden. The seaborne transit trade, which the port relied upon, collapsed with the temporary closure of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> and Britain's withdrawal from Aden in 1967. </p>
      <p>Since the conclusion of the war, the government made an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) to implement a <a href="/wiki/Structural_adjustment" title="Structural adjustment">structural adjustment</a> program. Phase one of the program included major financial and monetary reforms, including floating the currency, reducing the budget deficit, and cutting subsidies. Phase two addresses structural issues, such as civil service reform. </p>
      <p>In early 1995, the government of Yemen launched an economic, financial, and administrative reform program (EFARP) with the support of the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the IMF, as well as international donors. These programs had a positive impact on Yemen's economy and led to the reduction of the budget deficit to less than 3% of gross domestic product during the period 1995â1999 and the correction of macro-financial imbalances.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup> The real growth rate in the non-oil sector rose by 5.6% from 1995 to 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Yemen" title="Water supply and sanitation in Yemen">Water supply and sanitation in Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A key challenge is severe <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impacts_of_the_Yemeni_Civil_War_(2015%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental impacts of the Yemeni Civil War (2015âpresent)">water scarcity</a>, especially in the Highlands, prompting <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> to write "Yemen could become first nation to run out of water."<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> A second key challenge is a high level of poverty, making it difficult to recover the costs of service provision. Access to water supply sanitation is as low as in some sub-Saharan African countries. Yemen is both the poorest country and the most water-scarce country in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>. Third, the capacity of sector institutions to plan, build, operate and maintain infrastructure remains limited. Last but not least the security situation makes it even more difficult to improve or even maintain existing levels of service. </p>
      <p>The average Yemeni has access to only 140 cubic meters of water per year (101 gallons per day) for all uses, while the Middle Eastern average is 1000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>/yr, and the internationally defined threshold for water stress is 1700 cubic meters per year.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup> Yemen's groundwater is the main source of water in the country but the water tables have dropped severely leaving Yemen without a viable source of water. For example, in Sana'a, the water table was 30 metres (98 feet) below surface in the 1970s but had dropped to 1,200 metres (3,900 feet) below surface by 2012. The groundwater has not been regulated by Yemen's governments.<sup id="cite_ref-IRIN_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-334">[334]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Even before the revolution, Yemen's water situation had been described as increasingly dire by experts who worried that Yemen would be the first country to run out of water.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_Ecocentric_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time_Ecocentric-335">[335]</a></sup> Agriculture in Yemen takes up about 90% of water in Yemen even though it only generates 6% of GDP. A large portion of Yemenis are dependent on small-scale subsistence agriculture. Half of the agricultural water in Yemen is used to grow <a href="/wiki/Khat" title="Khat">khat</a>, a drug that many Yemenis chew. </p>
      <p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/2015_Yemeni_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 Yemeni Civil War">2015 Yemeni civil war</a>, the situation is increasingly dire. 80% of Yemen's population struggles to access water to drink and bathe. Bombing has forced many Yemenis to leave their homes for other areas, and so wells in those areas are under increasing pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPo_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo-336">[336]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Yemen" title="Demographics of Yemen">Demographics of Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Yemen's population is 28 million by 2018 estimates,<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-3">[3]</a></sup> with 46% of the population being under 15 years old and 2.7% above 65 years. In 1950, it was 4.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup> By 2050, the population is estimated to increase to about 60&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup> Yemen has a high <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a>, at 4.45 children per woman. It is the 30th highest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup> Sana'a's population has increased rapidly, from roughly 55,000 in 1978<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup> to nearly 2 million in the early 21st century. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yemen_ethno_2002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Yemen_ethno_2002.jpg/300px-Yemen_ethno_2002.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Yemen_ethno_2002.jpg/450px-Yemen_ethno_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Yemen_ethno_2002.jpg/600px-Yemen_ethno_2002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="951" data-file-height="985"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yemen_ethno_2002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Yemen's <a href="/wiki/Category:Yemeni_tribes" title="Category:Yemeni tribes">tribal areas</a> and Shia/Sunni regions. <a href="/wiki/Shia_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Muslims">Shia Muslims</a> predominant in the green area of Yemen's West, with the rest of Yemen being <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslims</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Yemeni ethnic groups are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Afro-Arab" title="Afro-Arab">Afro-Arabs</a>, South Asians and Europeans.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_325-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-325">[325]</a></sup> When the former states of North and South Yemen were established, most resident minority groups departed.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup> Yemen is a largely <a href="/wiki/Tribal" class="mw-redirect" title="Tribal">tribal</a> society.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup> In the northern, mountainous parts of the country, there are 400 Zaidi tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> There are also hereditary caste groups in urban areas such as <a href="/wiki/Al-Akhdam" title="Al-Akhdam">Al-Akhdam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lehmann_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lehmann-345">[345]</a></sup> There are also Yemenis of <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian people">Persian origin</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Muqaddasi" class="mw-redirect" title="Muqaddasi">Muqaddasi</a>, Persians formed the majority of Aden's population in the 10th century.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">[347]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Yemenite_Jews" title="Yemenite Jews">Yemenite Jews</a> once formed a sizable minority in Yemen with a distinct culture from other Jewish communities in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup> Most emigrated to <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> in the mid-20th century, following the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_Arab_and_Muslim_countries" title="Jewish exodus from Arab and Muslim countries">Jewish exodus from Arab and Muslim countries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Magic_Carpet_(Yemen)" title="Operation Magic Carpet (Yemen)">Operation Magic Carpet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">[349]</a></sup> An estimated 100,000 people of Indian origin are concentrated in the southern part of the country, around Aden, Mukalla, Shihr, Lahaj, Mokha and Hodeidah.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">[350]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most of the prominent <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Indonesia" title="Ethnic groups in Indonesia">Indonesians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysians" title="Malaysians">Malaysians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Singaporeans" title="Singaporeans">Singaporeans</a> of <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> descent are <a href="/wiki/Hadhrami_people" title="Hadhrami people">Hadhrami people</a> with origins in southern Yemen in the <a href="/wiki/Hadramawt" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadramawt">Hadramawt</a> coastal region.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup> Today there are almost 10,000 Hadramis in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">[352]</a></sup> The Hadramis migrated to Southeast Asia, East Africa and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">[353]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Maqil" title="Maqil">Maqil</a> were a collection of Arab <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> tribes of Yemeni origin who migrated westwards via <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>. Several groups of Yemeni Arabs turned south to <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>, and by the end of the 17th century, they dominated the entire country. They can also be found throughout Morocco and in Algeria as well as in other North African Countries.<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">[354]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Yemen is the only country in the Arabian Peninsula that is signatory to two international accords dating back to 1951 and 1967 governing the protection of refugees.<sup id="cite_ref-Jonathan_Fowler_355-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jonathan_Fowler-355">[355]</a></sup> Yemen hosted a population of refugees and asylum seekers numbering approximately 124,600 in 2007. Refugees and asylum seekers living in Yemen were predominantly from <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> (110,600), <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> (11,000), <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> (2,000),<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_305-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-305">[305]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Refugees of the Syrian civil war">Syria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">[356]</a></sup> Additionally, more than 334,000 Yemenis have been internally displaced by conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-Jonathan_Fowler_355-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jonathan_Fowler-355">[355]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_diaspora" title="Yemeni diaspora">Yemeni diaspora</a> is largely concentrated in neighbouring Saudi Arabia, where between 800,000 and 1 million Yemenis reside,<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">[357]</a></sup> and the United Kingdom, home to between <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_British" class="mw-redirect" title="Yemeni British">70,000 and 80,000</a> Yemenis.<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[358]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a> is the official language of Yemen, while <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_Arabic" title="Yemeni Arabic">Yemeni Arabic</a> is used as the vernacular. In <a href="/wiki/Al_Mahrah_Governorate" title="Al Mahrah Governorate">al Mahrah Governorate</a> in the far east and the island of <a href="/wiki/Socotra" title="Socotra">Socotra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_South_Arabian_languages" title="Modern South Arabian languages">several non-Arabic languages</a> are spoken.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[359]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">[360]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_Sign_Language" title="Yemeni Sign Language">Yemeni Sign Language</a> is used by the deaf community. </p>
      <p>Yemen is part of the homeland of the <a href="/wiki/South_Semitic_languages" title="South Semitic languages">South Semitic languages</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mehri_language" title="Mehri language">Mehri</a> is the largest South Semitic language spoken in the nation, with more than 70,000 speakers. The ethnic group itself is called Mahra. <a href="/wiki/Soqotri_language" title="Soqotri language">Soqotri</a> is another South Semitic language, with speakers on the island of Socotra isolated from the pressures of Arabic on the Yemeni mainland. According to the 1990 census in Yemen, the number of speakers there was 57,000.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[361]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Yemen was also home of the <a href="/wiki/Old_South_Arabian" title="Old South Arabian">Old South Arabian</a> languages. The <a href="/wiki/Razihi_language" title="Razihi language">Razihi language</a> appears to be the only remaining Old South Arabian language. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is the most important foreign language, being widely taught and spoken mostly in the south, a <a href="/wiki/Aden_Protectorate" title="Aden Protectorate">former British colony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">[362]</a></sup> There are a significant number of Russian speakers, originating from Yemeni-Russian cross-marriages occurring mainly in the 1970s and 1980s. A small <a href="/wiki/Cham_language" title="Cham language">Cham</a>-speaking community is found in the capital city of Sana'a, originating from refugees expatriated from Vietnam after the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> in the 1970s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_areas">Urban areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Urban areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Yemen" title="Religion in Yemen">Religion in Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Alsalh-24-2-2014_(16481824622).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Alsalh-24-2-2014_%2816481824622%29.jpg/220px-Alsalh-24-2-2014_%2816481824622%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Alsalh-24-2-2014_%2816481824622%29.jpg/330px-Alsalh-24-2-2014_%2816481824622%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Alsalh-24-2-2014_%2816481824622%29.jpg/440px-Alsalh-24-2-2014_%2816481824622%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2825" data-file-height="1656"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Alsalh-24-2-2014_(16481824622).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Saleh_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Saleh Mosque">Saleh Mosque</a> in Sana'a
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Islam is the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a> of Yemen. Religion in Yemen consists primarily of two principal <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> religious groups: About 55% of the Muslim population is <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> and 45% is <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a>, according to the International Religious Freedom Report.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[365]</a></sup> Sunnis are primarily <a href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafi'i">Shafi'i</a> but also include significant groups of <a href="/wiki/Maliki" title="Maliki">Malikis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hanbali" title="Hanbali">Hanbalis</a>. Shias are primarily <a href="/wiki/Zaydiyyah" class="mw-redirect" title="Zaydiyyah">Zaydi</a> and also have significant minorities of <a href="/wiki/Ismaili" class="mw-redirect" title="Ismaili">Ismaili</a><sup id="cite_ref-UNHRC_366-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHRC-366">[366]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Twelver" title="Twelver">Twelver</a><sup id="cite_ref-UNHRC_366-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHRC-366">[366]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup> Shias. </p>
      <p>The Sunnis are predominantly in the south and southeast. The Zaidis are predominantly in the north and northwest whilst the Ismailis are in the main centres such as Sana'a and Ma'rib. There are mixed communities in the larger cities. About .05 percent of Yemenis are non-Muslim â adhering to Christianity, <a href="/wiki/Yemenite_Jews" title="Yemenite Jews">Judaism</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Arab_states" title="Hinduism in Arab states">Hinduism</a> or having no religious affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Estimates of the number of <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Yemen" title="Christianity in Yemen">Christians in Yemen</a> range from 25,000<sup id="cite_ref-us_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us-370">[370]</a></sup> to 41,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Guide:_Christians_in_the_Middle_East_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guide:_Christians_in_the_Middle_East-371">[371]</a></sup> A 2015 study estimates 400 Christians from a Muslim background in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">[372]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are approximately 50 <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Yemeni Jews">Jews left in Yemen</a>. Some 200 Yemenite Jews were brought to Israel by the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish Agency">Jewish Agency</a> circa 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to WIN/Gallup International polls, Yemen has the most religious population among Arab countries and it is one of the most religious population world-wide.<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Yemen" title="Culture of Yemen">Culture of Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sana%27a_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Sana%27a_Museum.jpg/220px-Sana%27a_Museum.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Sana%27a_Museum.jpg/330px-Sana%27a_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Sana%27a_Museum.jpg/440px-Sana%27a_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1721" data-file-height="1147"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sana%27a_Museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The National Museum in Sana'a
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yemeni_House_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Yemeni_House_1.jpg/220px-Yemeni_House_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Yemeni_House_1.jpg/330px-Yemeni_House_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Yemeni_House_1.jpg/440px-Yemeni_House_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a>

         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yemeni_House_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Typical Yemeni House
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sa%27dah_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Sa%27dah_05.jpg/220px-Sa%27dah_05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Sa%27dah_05.jpg/330px-Sa%27dah_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Sa%27dah_05.jpg/440px-Sa%27dah_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3335" data-file-height="2088"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sa%27dah_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dance in <a href="/wiki/Sa%27dah" title="Sa'dah">Sa'dah</a>, northwestern Yemen
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Yemen is a culturally rich country with influence from many civilizations, such as the early civilization of <a href="/wiki/Sabaeans" title="Sabaeans">Saba'</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Burrowes2010_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burrowes2010-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Simpson2002_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson2002-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kitchen2003_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kitchen2003-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Yemen">Media of Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Radio_in_Yemen" title="Radio in Yemen">Radio broadcasting in Yemen</a> began in the 1940s when it was still divided into the South by the British and the North by the <a href="/wiki/Yahya_Muhammad_Hamid_ed-Din" title="Yahya Muhammad Hamid ed-Din">Imami ruling system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">[375]</a></sup> After the unification of Yemen in 1990, the Yemeni government reformed its corporations and founded some additional radio stations that broadcast locally. However, it drew back after 1994, due to destroyed infrastructure resulting from <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_Civil_War_(1994)" title="Yemeni Civil War (1994)">the civil war</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Television_in_Yemen" title="Television in Yemen">Television</a> is the most significant media platform in Yemen. Given the low literacy rate in the country, television is the main source of news for Yemenis. There are six free-to-air channels currently headquartered in Yemen, of which four are state-owned.<sup id="cite_ref-amo12_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amo12-376">[376]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Yemen" title="Cinema of Yemen">Yemeni film industry</a> is in its early stages; only two Yemeni films have been released as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Theatre_in_Yemen" title="Theatre in Yemen">Theatre in Yemen</a>
      </div>
      <p> The history of Yemeni theatre dates back at least a century, to the early 1900s. Both amateur and professional (government-sponsored) theatre troupes perform in the country's major urban centres. Many of Yemen's significant poets and authors, like Ali Ahmed Ba Kathir, Muhammad al-Sharafi, and <a href="/wiki/Wajdi_al-Ahdal" title="Wajdi al-Ahdal">Wajdi al-Ahdal</a>, have written dramatic works; poems, novels, and short stories by Yemeni authors like <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Abdul-Wali" title="Mohammad Abdul-Wali">Mohammad Abdul-Wali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abdulaziz_Al-Maqaleh" title="Abdulaziz Al-Maqaleh">Abdulaziz Al-Maqaleh</a> have also been adapted for the stage. There have been Yemeni productions of plays by Arab authors such as <a href="/wiki/Tawfiq_al-Hakim" title="Tawfiq al-Hakim">Tawfiq al-Hakim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saadallah_Wannous" title="Saadallah Wannous">Saadallah Wannous</a> and by Western authors, including <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Pirandello" title="Luigi Pirandello">Pirandello</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Brecht">Brecht</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Williams" title="Tennessee Williams">Tennessee Williams</a>. Historically speaking, the southern port city of Aden is the cradle of Yemeni theatre; in recent decades the capital, Sana'a, has hosted numerous theatre festivals, often in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/World_Theatre_Day" title="World Theatre Day">World Theatre Day</a>. </p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>

      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Yemen. The <a href="/wiki/Yemen_Football_Association" title="Yemen Football Association">Yemen Football Association</a> is a member of <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">AFC</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Yemen_national_football_team" title="Yemen national football team">Yemeni national football team</a> participates internationally. The country also hosts many football clubs. They compete in the national and international leagues. </p>
      <p>Yemen's mountains provide many opportunities for outdoor sports, such as <a href="/wiki/Mountain_biking" title="Mountain biking">biking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing" title="Rock climbing">rock climbing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trekking" class="mw-redirect" title="Trekking">trekking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a>, and other more challenging sports, including <a href="/wiki/Mountain_climbing" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain climbing">mountain climbing</a>. Mountain climbing and hiking tours to the <a href="/wiki/Sarawat_Mountains" title="Sarawat Mountains">Sarawat Mountains</a>, including peaks of 3,000&nbsp;m (9,800&nbsp;ft) and above, particularly that of An-Nabi Shu'ayb,<sup id="cite_ref-Burrows2010_281-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burrows2010-281">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Laughlin2008_284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laughlin2008-284">[284]</a></sup> are seasonally organized by local and international alpine agencies. </p>
      <p>The coastal areas of Yemen and <a href="/wiki/Socotra" title="Socotra">Socotra Island</a> also provide many opportunities for water sports, such as <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bodyboarding" title="Bodyboarding">bodyboarding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sailing_(sport)" title="Sailing (sport)">sailing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a>. Socotra Island is home to some of the best surfing destinations in the world. </p>
      <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Camel_jumping&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Camel jumping (page does not exist)">Camel jumping</a> is a traditional sport that is becoming increasingly popular among the Zaraniq tribe on the west coast of Yemen in a desert plain by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>. Camels are placed side to side and victory goes to the competitor who leaps, from a running start, over the most camels. The jumpers train year round for competitions. Tribesmen (women may not compete) tuck their robes around their waists for freedom of movement while running and leaping.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">[377]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Yemen's biggest sports event was hosting the <a href="/wiki/20th_Arabian_Gulf_Cup" title="20th Arabian Gulf Cup">20th Arabian Gulf Cup</a> in Aden and Abyan in the southern part of the country on 22 November 2010. Many thought Yemen was the strongest competitor, but it was defeated in the first three matches of the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">[378]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Internationally, <a href="/wiki/Naseem_Hamed" title="Naseem Hamed">Naseem Hamed</a>, a world champion boxer, is the most well known Yemeni athlete. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Heritage_sites">World Heritage sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: World Heritage sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Yemen" title="Tourism in Yemen">Tourism in Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg/220px-Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg/330px-Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg/440px-Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1320"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Shibam_Wadi_Hadhramaut_Yemen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>High-rise architecture at <a href="/wiki/Shibam" class="mw-redirect" title="Shibam">Shibam</a>, Wadi <a href="/wiki/Hadramawt" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadramawt">Hadramawt</a>â
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Among Yemen's natural and cultural attractions are four <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage">World Heritage</a> sites.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_WHC_2015_379-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO_WHC_2015-379">[379]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_WHC_2015_B_380-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO_WHC_2015_B-380">[380]</a></sup> The Old Walled City of <a href="/wiki/Shibam" class="mw-redirect" title="Shibam">Shibam</a> in Wadi Hadhramaut, inscribed by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 1982, two years after Yemen joined the World Heritage Committee, is nicknamed "Manhattan of the Desert" because of its skyscrapers. Surrounded by a fortified wall made of mud and straw, the 16th-century city is one of the oldest examples of urban planning based on the principle of vertical construction. </p>
      <p>The Old City of Sana'a, at an altitude of more than 2,100 metres (7,000&nbsp;ft), has been inhabited for over two and a half millennia, and was inscribed in 1986. Sana'a became a major Islamic centre in the 7th century, and the 103 mosques, 14 hammams (traditional bathhouses), and more than 6,000 houses that survive all date from before the 11th century. </p>
      <p>Close to the Red Sea Coast, the historic town of <a href="/wiki/Zabid" title="Zabid">Zabid</a>, inscribed in 1993, was Yemen's capital from the 13th to the 15th century, and is an archaeological and historical site. It played an important role for many centuries because of its university, which was a centre of learning for the whole Arab and Islamic world. Algebra is said to have been invented there in the early 9th century by the little-known scholar <a href="/wiki/Al-Jazari" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Jazari">Al-Jazari</a>. </p>
      <p>The latest addition to Yemen's list of World Heritage Sites is the <a href="/wiki/Socotra" title="Socotra">Socotra</a> Archipelago. Mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> in the 13th century, this remote and isolated archipelago consists of four islands and two rocky islets delineating the southern limit of the Gulf of Aden. The site has a rich biodiversity. Nowhere else in the world do 37% of Socotra's 825 plants, 90% of its reptiles and 95% of its snails occur. It is home to 192 bird species, 253 species of coral, 730 species of coastal fish, and 300 species of crab and lobster, as well as a range of <i><a href="/wiki/Aloe" title="Aloe">Aloes</a></i> and the Dragon's Blood Tree (<i><a href="/wiki/Dracaena_cinnabari" title="Dracaena cinnabari">Dracaena cinnabari</a></i>). The cultural heritage of Socotra includes the unique <a href="/wiki/Soqotri_language" title="Soqotri language">Soqotri language</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Yemen" title="Education in Yemen">Education in Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UIS_Literacy_Rate_Yemen_population_plus15_1995-2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Yemen_population_plus15_1995-2015.png/220px-UIS_Literacy_Rate_Yemen_population_plus15_1995-2015.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Yemen_population_plus15_1995-2015.png/330px-UIS_Literacy_Rate_Yemen_population_plus15_1995-2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fa/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Yemen_population_plus15_1995-2015.png 2x" data-file-width="398" data-file-height="319"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:UIS_Literacy_Rate_Yemen_population_plus15_1995-2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Literacy rate of the population aged 15 or older (1995â2015) by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> Institute of Statistics
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The adult literacy rate in 2010 was 64%.<sup id="cite_ref-unescolit_381-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unescolit-381">[381]</a></sup> The government has committed to reduce illiteracy to less than 10% by 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">[382]</a></sup> Although Yemen's government provides for universal, compulsory, free education for children ages six through 15, the U.S. Department of State reports that compulsory attendance is not enforced. The government developed the National Basic Education Development Strategy in 2003 that aimed at providing education to 95% of Yemeni children between the ages of six and 14 years and also at decreasing the gap between males and females in urban and rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">[383]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A seven-year project to improve gender equity and the quality and efficiency of secondary education, focusing on girls in rural areas, was approved by the World Bank in March 2008. Following this, Yemen has increased its education spending from 5% of GDP in 1995 to 10% in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-YemenProfile2008_224-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YemenProfile2008-224">[224]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a>, the top-ranking universities in the country are the <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_University_of_Science_%26_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Yemeni University of Science &amp; Technology">Yemeni University of Science &amp; Technology</a> (6532nd worldwide), Al Ahgaff University (8930th) and <a href="/wiki/Sanaa_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanaa University">Sanaa University</a> (11043rd).<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">[384]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Yemen" title="Health in Yemen">Health in Yemen</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Famine_in_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Famine in Yemen">Famine in Yemen</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Yemen_cholera_outbreak" class="mw-redirect" title="2016â17 Yemen cholera outbreak">2016â17 Yemen cholera outbreak</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yemeni_doctor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Yemeni_doctor.jpg/220px-Yemeni_doctor.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Yemeni_doctor.jpg/330px-Yemeni_doctor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Yemeni_doctor.jpg/440px-Yemeni_doctor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2371" data-file-height="2211"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yemeni_doctor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Yemeni doctor examines an infant in a USAID-sponsored health care clinic
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite the significant progress Yemen has made to expand and improve its health care system over the past decade, the system remains severely underdeveloped. Total expenditures on health care in 2002 constituted 3.7 percent of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_385-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-385">[385]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In that same year, the per capita expenditure for health care was very low, as compared with other <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle Eastern</a> countriesâUS$58 according to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> statistics and US$23 according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the number of <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">doctors</a> in Yemen rose by an average of more than 7 percent between 1995 and 2000, but as of 2004 there were still only three doctors per 10,000 persons. In 2003 Yemen had only 0.6 hospital beds available per 1,000 persons.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_385-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-385">[385]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Health care services are particularly scarce in rural areas. Only 25 percent of rural areas are covered by health services, as compared with 80 percent of urban areas. <a href="/wiki/Emergency_services" class="mw-redirect" title="Emergency services">Emergency services</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Ambulance" title="Ambulance">ambulance</a> service and <a href="/wiki/Blood_banks" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood banks">blood banks</a>, are non-existent.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_385-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-385">[385]</a></sup> </p>
